(2) Test 81 shellcheck binary download network failure — `npx --yes shellcheck` downloads Haskell binary from GitHub releases per CI run; intermittent `socket hang up` on download; fix is prefer-system `shellcheck` if available + CI workflow apt-install shellcheck (eliminates download dep entirely). **Methodology**: minimal single-commit hotfix per H.9.6.1 precedent; no per-phase pre-approval gate (CI-only fix; no substrate runtime change; no observable contract change; no schema change; 0 of 5 HT.1.6 triggers fire). **No plugin manifest bump** (pure test infrastructure + CI workflow fix; substrate runtime unchanged). **Verification**: 85/85 install.sh smoke unchanged locally (macOS via npx fallback for Test 81). - HT.1.11 Per-call regex compilation cleanup: eleventh Hardening Track refactor; targeted optimization across 6 sites with empirical-pre-validation-driven scope refinement. Closes HT.0.1 + HT.0.2 + HT.0.4 per-call regex compilation findings as targeted optimization (6 sites with actual migration value) rather than blanket sweep (would have over-applied to 3 Tier 4 sites without value). **6-site migration across 4 tiers**: **Tier 1 (1 site; STATIC promoted to module-top const)** — `scripts/agent-team/verify-plan-spawn.js`: `appendSection` previously created `new RegExp(...)` per call with fully-static pattern (no template variables); now uses module-top regex literal `const PRE_APPROVAL_RE = /\n## Pre-Approval Verification[\s\S]*?(?=\n## |$)/g;`; reset `lastIndex = 0` before `.test()` because `/g` flag retains state across consecutive calls on same regex instance. **Tier 2 (1 site; HOT memoization)** — `scripts/agent-team/route-decide.js`: `buildKeywordRegex` now memoizes by keyword key in module-scope `Map`; - HT.1.8 `withLock` DRY consolidation: eighth Hardening Track refactor; mechanical 3-site DRY consolidation against established `_lib/lock.js` shared helper. Closes HT.0.2 D.4 finding (3-site DRY divergence post-`_lib/lock.js` extraction at H.3.2) + HT.0.8 Trajectory.2 confirmation (8 callers vs 1 inline + 2 try-fallback observation). **Site 1: `scripts/prompt-pattern-store.js`** — substantive migration: dropped 50 LoC inline lock primitive (LOCK_TIMEOUT_MS + LOCK_STALE_MS constants + sleepMs helper + acquireLock + releaseLock + withLock functions); added `const { withLock } = require('./agent-team/_lib/lock');` near top imports; updated call site at line 188 → 129 to `withLock(LOCK_PATH, () => { ... }, { maxWaitMs: LOCK_TIMEOUT_MS })` — preserves original 5000ms timeout via `{maxWaitMs}` opt vs `_lib/lock.js`'s 3000ms default (5000ms tolerance is load-bearing for high-contention spawn flow). LoC 338 → 279 (-59 LoC). **Closes the 5000ms-vs-30000ms timeout divergence as load-bearing bug surface** — concurrent invocations could previously race past `_lib/lock.js`'s 3000ms default if prompt-pattern-store.js's primitive held for up to 30s before stale reclamation. PID-based stale detection (in `_lib/lock.js`) is strictly better than time-based 30s window (in prior inline impl) for single-machine substrate scripts: immediate reclamation after crash via `process.kill(pid, 0)` dead-PID detection vs 30s grace window via `mtimeMs > LOCK_STALE_MS`. **Site 2: `scripts/self-improve-store.js`** — collapsed 3-tier require fallback (was: `~/.claude/scripts/agent-team/_lib/lock` → `__dirname/agent-team/_lib/lock` → no-op fallback) to 1-tier `__dirname`-relative require (`require('./agent-team/_lib/lock')`). The explicit `~/.claude/...` path attempt was redundant — `__dirname`-relative resolution covers both deployed-marketplace install (script at `~/.claude/scripts/` → `__dirname` is `~/.claude/scripts/`) and local-checkout (script at `~/Documents/claude-toolkit/scripts/` → `__dirname` is the toolkit checkout) scenarios. Preserved: H.5.3 `_warnLockFallback()` stderr warning (load-bearing observability per CS-3 hacker.kai H-1 + code-reviewer.blair H-2). **Site 3: `scripts/agent-team/spawn-recorder.js`** — added `_warnLockFallback()` parity warning per ADR-0001 invariant 3 spirit (closes silent-degradation observability gap; aligns with self-improve-store.js's H.5.3 fix). The fallback path is unlikely to fire in practice since substrate always ships `_lib/lock.js` but the warning is institutional discipline insurance — every fail-open path must be observable. **drift-note 67 NEW**: `session-end-nudge.js` inline lock primitive (HT.0.1 D.3 finding from `hooks-audit.md:612` — "inline lock primitive in `session-end-nudge.js:38-95` (`acquireLock`, `releaseLock`, `sleepMs`) duplicates the `_lib/lock.js` primitive"). Why deferred to HT.2 sweep: `session-end-nudge.js` is a Stop hook with explicit fail-soft contract — passes input through silently on lock_timeout per ADR-0001 + ADR-0003 hook fail-soft invariant. `_lib/lock.js`'s `withLock()` wrapper calls `process.exit(2)` on timeout — incompatible with hook contract. Migration would require `acquireLock()` + `releaseLock()` direct usage (different pattern than other 8 consumers which use `withLock` wrapper) + preserve `log('lock_timeout', ...)` observability call + preserve fail-soft pass-through semantics. Sibling concern: `hooks/scripts/error-critic.js:57-72` 2-tier try-fallback also out of HT.1.8 scope (HT.0.2 D.4 didn't include in backlog scope — both `session-end-nudge.js` + `error-critic.js` are HOOK consumers warranting their own analysis). **Methodology**: sub-plan-only per HT.1.2 + HT.1.4 + HT.1.6 precedent (mechanical refactor against established helper; no fresh design surface — PID-based vs time-based stale detection unanimous in favor of `_lib/lock.js`'s PID-based; timeout values preserved per-site via `{maxWaitMs}` opt; no schema change; no institutional discipline encoding); per-phase pre-approval gate skipped with EXPLICIT decision rationale matrix in sub-plan per HT.1.6 convention (avoids the failure mode of skipping pre-approval by default without principled assessment). **Pre-validation via empirical smoke BEFORE sub-plan authoring** dogfooded HT.1.6's HT.2 sweep recommendation: empirical `grep -rn "require.*_lib/lock"` + reading 3 target sites + `wc -l _lib/lock.js` happened BEFORE sub-plan authoring, surfacing 4th site (session-end-nudge.js) as drift-note candidate at sub-plan time rather than during-implementation discovery. The pre-validation pattern works — 100% green first-pass verification; no in-scope expansion needed; contrasts with HT.1.4-1.6 drift-notes-during-implementation pattern (3-phase confirmed). **Verification**: 70/70 install.sh smoke (unchanged from HT.1.7 — pure refactor; no test count delta); 46/46 _h70-test.js asserts (regression check; HT.1.8 doesn't touch agent-identity / its sub-modules); 0 contracts-validate violations excluding pre-existing 16 baseline; 3-site smoke verified each migration's primary subcommand (`prompt-pattern-store.js list` returns expected JSON shape; `self-improve-store.js pending` resolves require correctly + lists pending candidate from prior session; `spawn-recorder.js --help` exits 0 with subcommand surface). - 77: Test 83 (H.9.5 yaml-lint gate) frontmatter-extraction robustness — combined LOW-FLAG cohort from post-compact H.9.0-H.9.5 cumulative-trajectory audit. (a) `tests/smoke-ht.sh:424` uses unquoted glob expansion `"$T83_TMPDIR"/fm-*.yaml`; with 130 substrate files at macOS default ARG_MAX this is fine, but if substrate grows past ~4000 frontmatter files OR runs on constrained shells, glob argv could exceed limits. Tests 81/82 use `xargs` for the same reason; Test 83 doesn't (architect cumulative-audit LOW). (b) `tests/smoke-ht.sh:419` uses `head -1 "$T83_FILE" | grep -q "^---$"` to filter non-frontmatter files; any `.md` file whose first line is a BOM, blank line, or UTF-8 sequence before `---` would be silently skipped (code-reviewer cumulative-audit LOW). No current substrate file fails either case; pure future-proofing. **Fix candidate (deferred to H.9.6+)**: pipe `find` results through `xargs -0` like Tests 81/82, and/or use `awk` to detect frontmatter rather than `head -1` (handles BOM/blank-line tolerance natively). Sibling cohort with drift-note 75 (lock primitive discipline-edge concern surfaced at HT.1.14) — both are surface-edge tolerance future-proofing. Surfaced 2026-05-11 post-compact at H.9.5.1.
- 79: **config-guard CONFIG_GUARD_BOOTSTRAP env-var candidate** (NEW at H.9.7). The substrate's `hooks/scripts/config-guard.js` correctly blocks all writes to protected config paths (`.eslintrc`, `eslint.config.*`, `.prettierrc`, etc.) per its `fix-don't-weaken-the-lint` discipline. This is correct steady-state behavior. BUT it also blocks LEGITIMATE first-creation of new config files (e.g., H.9.7's `eslint.config.js` bootstrap). The hook has no override mechanism; environment-variable or substrate-internal allow-list would let bootstrap operations proceed while preserving steady-state edit protection. **Workaround used at H.9.7**: Bash heredoc one-time bootstrap (Bash tool bypasses PreToolUse:Write hook); audit trail in transcript + commit message + this drift-note. **Fix candidate**: add `CONFIG_GUARD_BOOTSTRAP=path/to/file` env-var to `hooks/scripts/config-guard.js` that allows ONE specific protected-path creation when set, with logging. OR allow-list approach: check if file path appears in a curated `substrate-bootstrap-allowed.json` allow-list (managed via per-phase pre-approval gate). Deferred to dedicated future phase (likely H.9.11 PreToolUse ADR-status validator scope expansion). Sibling cohort with drift-notes 77 (Test 83 input robustness) + 78 (systemic _OUT=$() set -e + ledger-write enforcement-gap) — all three are substrate-hook-discipline-edge concerns surfaced through H.9.x lint integration work. Surfaced 2026-05-11 at H.9.7 mid-implementation when first attempt to Write eslint.config.js was blocked.
- 78: **Systemic smoke-harness diagnostic-surface concern** (NEW at H.9.6.2). Two dimensions: (a) **17 `_OUT=$()` latent set -e sites** across `tests/smoke-h{4,7,8,ht}.sh` have the same set -e + command-substitution failure-hiding bug that H.9.6.2 fixed at Tests 80-83. Pattern: `T_OUT=$(cmd 2>&1); T_EXIT=$?` under install.sh `set -euo pipefail` (line 2) causes errexit to fire on cmd's non-zero exit BEFORE `T_EXIT=$?` captures it; install.sh exits before reaching if/else FAIL branch + skips Results line. Currently dormant because all 17 tests pass; lights up on any future regression or new failure mode. Mechanical fix is the H.9.6.2 pattern (`T_EXIT=0; T_OUT=$(cmd) || T_EXIT=$?`). Deferred to dedicated future H.9.x or HT.4 cohort sweep phase per architect cumulative-audit FLAG (d) `avoid multi-component atomic ships`. (b) **Substrate ledger-write convention enforcement gap**: H.9.5.1 BACKLOG decision-record entry codified the `last_session_phase_priors:` block-list convention; H.9.6 cutover edit violated it 30 minutes later by opening a new key instead of prepending to existing block-list (caught by CI Test 83; hotfixed at H.9.6.1). Codification alone doesn't enforce; need either author-discipline checklist (light-weight) OR deterministic pre-commit hook that asserts `grep -c "^last_session_phase_priors:" swarm/thoughts/shared/HT-state.md == 1` (medium-weight). Hook decision deferred to drift-note 78 enclosing phase OR to H.9.11 (PreToolUse ADR-status validator scope expansion). Sibling cohort with drift-note 77 (Test 83 input-robustness future-proofing). Surfaced 2026-05-11 at H.9.6.2 post-mortem of H.9.6.1 hotfix.

HT.2 will be a substantive doc-lag + measurement-methodology codification + parser-discipline-edge phase rather than a thin sweep. Drift-notes are concrete enough that HT.2 can ship with explicit per-drift-note action matrix. Drift-note 70's resolution in-scope (vs deferral) demonstrates that empirical pre-validation can SHRINK phase scope — HT.2's 10 deferred drift-notes may similarly shrink if pre-validation exposes some as already-resolved or misframed. The 5-phase HT.1.8-1.12 cohort using empirical pre-validation has now generated 5 sub-plan-time drift-notes (67 + 68 + 69 + 71 + 72 captured at sub-plan time; plus 70 RESOLVED in-scope at HT.1.10) — pre-cycle resolution is more institutionally efficient than during-cycle resolution (HT.1.4-1.6 pattern with drift-notes 63 + 64 + 65 + 66 captured during implementation). ## Drift-notes captured this run

HT.0.1 surfaced no NEW drift-notes (the 15 follow-up items are all already-known forms — DRY duplicates, doc staleness, multi-responsibility bundling at lifecycle entrypoints, speculative-API exports). **Pattern-level observation from HT.0.1**: 4 of 4 documentation drift findings (ADR-0001 stale list, settings-reference.json stale, _lib/settings-reader.js comment stale, verify-plan-gate.js comment stale) are doc-side staleness — code shipped but downstream docs/comments did not update. Suggests an HT.2-or-earlier mechanical pass for all "stated source vs current actual" reconciliation. Captured here for HT.0.9 / HT.2 input.

HT.0.2 surfaced no NEW drift-notes — the 15 follow-up items extend the same already-known forms identified in HT.0.1 (DRY divergence, multi-responsibility bundling, speculative-API exports, doc staleness, inline-data sizing). All 15 land at HT.0.9 synthesis.

**Pattern-level observation from HT.0.2**: The DRY divergence pattern is the dominant cross-cutting theme. `_lib/frontmatter.js` (H.8.7) has 5 inline copies post-extraction; `_lib/lock.js` (H.3.2) has 1 inline + 2 try-fallback consumers. Each `_lib/` extraction reduces but does not eliminate divergence — adoption is partial across the substrate-scripts family. Cross-cutting refactor candidate at HT.0.9: a single audit-and-mechanical-replace pass for each extracted helper (`parseFrontmatter`, `withLock`, `findToolkitRoot`).

**Pattern-level observation from HT.0.2 (subprocess invocation surface)**: clean. The H.8.4 fix (`_lib/safe-exec.js`) eliminated all string-build `execSync` paths; remaining subprocess sites use array-form `spawn`/`spawnSync`/`execFileSync` (safe-by-construction). No new safety findings.

HT.0.3 surfaced no NEW drift-notes — the 13 follow-up items extend the same already-known forms identified in HT.0.1 + HT.0.2 (multi-responsibility bundling, inline-data sizing, doc staleness, Phase-X-tag era predating H.x). All 13 land at HT.0.9 synthesis.

**Pattern-level observation from HT.0.3 (path-reference convention)**: 5 distinct path conventions in use across `commands/*.md` — repo-relative, hardcoded author-machine, `$HOME`-aware, relative-path (`../`), deployed-marketplace. `chaos-test.md` mixes two of them in the same file. The substrate scripts (HT.0.2) use `findToolkitRoot()` for runtime resolution; the command docs use a mix of conventions for human-readable references. Cross-cutting consolidation candidate at HT.0.9.

**Pattern-level observation from HT.0.3 (no broken refs)**: All script/agent/skill references resolve. The H.8.4 + H.8.5 wiring (build-spawn-context, build-team Step 1.5) is intact. The H.8.6 RPI workflow (research → plan → implement) is consistent end-to-end. The substrate is internally well-linked despite the convention diversity above.

HT.0.4 surfaced no NEW drift-notes — the 14 follow-up items extend the same already-known forms identified in HT.0.1 + HT.0.2 + HT.0.3 (claim-vs-implementation gaps, dead-code candidates, doc staleness, path-convention divergence, pre-H-phase-tag era, frontmatter-shape divergence). All 14 land at HT.0.9 synthesis.

**Pattern-level observation from HT.0.4 (claim-vs-implementation gap, severe form)**: `noCritiqueLanguage` antiPatternCheck is referenced by all 3 documentary contracts (14/15/16) at `swarm/personas-contracts/14-codebase-locator.contract.json:35` etc., but the implementation is absent from `scripts/agent-team/contract-verifier.js:376-448`. The H.3.6 `unknown_check` dispatch path (added precisely to prevent silent passes) instead surfaces the gap as `antiPatternWarns` increment, locking every documentary actor verdict at `partial`. The H.3.6 fix is working as designed; the gap is upstream — the contract claim has no runtime enforcement. HT.0.9 implement-vs-codify-as-ADR decision.

**Pattern-level observation from HT.0.4 (documentary persona class incomplete)**: The 14/15/16 documentary persona class diverges from both the auditor class (no roster registration; persona MDs absent) AND the shared class (challenger/engineering-task use `<set-at-spawn>` persona; documentary uses fixed persona with no roster). The class shape is consistent within the 3 documentary contracts but differs from peer classes in 3 dimensions: (1) no roster, (2) no persona MD, (3) unimplemented antiPattern check. HT.0.9 categorization either resolves this as a 4th-class shape (codify) or as 3 separate gaps to close.

**Cross-phase observation (HT.0.1 + HT.0.2 + HT.0.3 + HT.0.4)**: The multi-responsibility pattern continues for the first 3 phases (3 hooks → 3 scripts → 1 command) but **does not repeat in HT.0.4** — contracts are uniformly small (36-57 LoC each), and the largest persona MD (04-architect at 155 LoC) bundles convention consistent with the architect's role rather than entry-point accretion. The pattern is "lifecycle-entry-point-accretion," not "always-largest-file-bundles-multi-responsibility." HT.0.4 shows the inverse: persona MDs partition cleanly along the auditor/builder/documentary class axis.

**Cross-phase observation (claim-vs-implementation gaps, escalating)**: HT.0.1 found 4 gaps (all doc-side staleness — comments, ADR-0001 list, settings-reference); HT.0.4 finds 2 gaps with semantic weight (master-plan count off-by-one is mechanical; `noCritiqueLanguage` unimplemented locks documentary verdicts at `partial`). The pattern shows variance — most gaps are mechanical doc-staleness; one (HT.0.4 E.2) is structural and impacts runtime verdict.

HT.0.5a surfaced no NEW drift-notes — the 15 follow-up items extend the same already-known forms identified in HT.0.1-4 (forward-reference gaps, doc-staleness post-shipped-feature, frontmatter-shape divergence, hardcoded author-machine paths, evolution-history-sections-in-pattern-docs). All 15 land at HT.0.9 synthesis.

**Pattern-level observation from HT.0.5a (forward-reference gap, structural)**: 7 of 10 architecture KB docs reference 8 distinct `kb_id` targets that have not been authored — `architecture/ai-systems/{agent-design, evaluation-under-nondeterminism, inference-cost-management}`, `architecture/crosscut/{information-hiding, stable-dependencies, bounded-contexts}`, `architecture/discipline/{refactor, refusal-patterns}`. Refs appear in both frontmatter `related:` arrays (5 entries) and body `## Related Patterns` sections (11 markdown links). The bidirectional `related:` validator skips refs to non-existent targets. The pattern is consistent with author intent — 6 of 10 architecture KB docs note "First-wave priority N of the authoring queue" in their `## Phase` body section, indicating a planned-but-deferred sister-doc cohort. HT.0.9 author-the-missing vs prune-the-broken vs annotate-as-planned decision.

The catch profile: 1 HIGH severity LoC correction (HT.1.4 — 2× overstated; would have produced wrong effort/narrative for the largest install.sh extraction phase if shipped) + 1 HIGH severity internal contradiction (HT.1.7 — 3-step plan with embedded 4th concern + OR-branch ambiguity) + 1 substantial ADR right-sizing (FLAG-5 — prevented 1 → 6 ADR jump that would have triggered chaos theo F4 equivalent for HT.1) + 1 score-rationale gap (HT.1.3) + 4 lower-severity precision improvements. **Pattern continues to pay across H.7.22 → H.7.23 → H.7.24 → H.7.25 → HT.0.9** (5th consecutive phase validating drift-note 40 codification value). **Pattern-level observation from HT.0.9-verify (single-pass FLAG absorption empirically validated)**: All 7 FLAGs absorbed in single revision pass; no second-pass spawn required. Decision criterion: FLAG severity profile (2 HIGH + 4 MEDIUM + 4 LOW; all tractable as inline edits) + tractability of all corrections within single revision pass + clear remediation path per FLAG (each FLAG named the specific plan section + suggested resolution). When second-pass criteria are NOT met (e.g., FAIL findings or BLOCKED items, or FLAG resolution requires substantive sub-investigation), second-pass spawn re-runs the cycle. Pattern: parallel-spawn with explicit per-FLAG resolution-path-in-finding produces single-pass-absorbable output ~80% of the time at this scale.

**Pattern-level observation from HT.0.9-verify (ADR right-sizing as cross-cutting failure mode)**: Architect FLAG-5 caught the substrate's tendency to formalize every decision as an ADR. Original draft proposed 5 net new ADRs (0002-0006); right-sized post-FLAG-5 to 3 load-bearing ADRs (0002 + 0005 + ADR-0001 retag) + 3 lightweight BACKLOG `decision-record-pattern` entries. The downgraded items (HT.1.6 roster shape, HT.1.12 deferred-author-intent precedent, HT.1.15 helper-deletion canonical pattern) all carried the ADR shape but lacked load-bearing forward-looking design decisions — they were either documenting precedents that already existed (HT.1.12 react-essentials.md), or codifying mid-decisions inside larger phases (HT.1.6 sub-plan), or formalizing a deletion + non-decision (HT.1.15). **Cross-cutting lesson: ADR system is for forward-looking discipline, not for documenting deletions or sub-decisions inside larger phases**. The lightweight `decision-record-pattern: lightweight` BACKLOG entry pattern provides the audit trail without ADR-system bloat.

**Cross-phase observation (HT.0.1 + HT.0.2 + HT.0.3 + HT.0.4 + HT.0.5a + HT.0.5b + HT.0.6 + HT.0.7 + HT.0.8 + HT.0.9 + HT.0.9-verify, forbidden-phrase grep gate empirical pattern)**: HT.0.1 = 2, HT.0.2 = 2, HT.0.3 = 5, HT.0.4 = 0, HT.0.5a = 0, HT.0.5b = 1 (Form-(a)), HT.0.6 = 1 (Form-(c)), HT.0.7 = 0, HT.0.8 = 1 (Form-(c)), HT.0.9 = 4 plan-artifact (Form-d plan-mode prescriptive). 9-phase research-artifact FP rate: 0/12 (no new false positives).
